> An example for clarification.  I own the domain "keithl.com", which
> is currently pointed at the IP address 72.249.22.145, along with a
> dozen other URLs .  Let's say I start up a new server on IP address
> 123.45.67.89, and copy the site information to that, and then turn
> on Apache.  The new server can respond to requests for all the 
> different virtuals, but DNS doesn't point to it yet.  I want to test
> keithl.com, and all the other virtuals, before I switch the DNS over.
> 
> THE QUESTION:  Is there some way to ask Firefox for, say,
> http://123.45.67.89:www.keithl.com/ , so that the browser goes
> to the right IP address and Apache gets the right browser information,
> as if DNS was actually pointing there? 
> 
> Yes, I can fake out the DNS on my own browser machine, but I would
> like a technique that I can use on another machine that I do not
> control, to make sure the new IP address is reachable before I change
> the DNS server to point to it.

Could you employ a reverse proxy?

:ducks:

From ron at Opus1.COM  Fri Nov 30 21:26:02 2007
From: ron at Opus1.COM (Ronald Chmara)
Date: Fri, 30 Nov 2007 21:26:02 -0800
Subject: [PLUG] Browser redirection for site testing
In-Reply-To: <20071130171007.GB26930@gate.kl-ic.com>
References: <20071130032655.GC14494@gate.kl-ic.com>
	<30537.192.136.50.130.1196395891.squirrel@sm.tbruce.com>
	<31426.192.136.50.130.1196396411.squirrel@sm.tbruce.com>
	<20071130171007.GB26930@gate.kl-ic.com>
Message-ID: <AF4D5334-5C52-4BB8-AF69-2048BD94BD02@opus1.com>


On Nov 30, 2007, at 9:10 AM, Keith Lofstrom wrote:

> On Thu, November 29, 2007 19:26, Keith Lofstrom said:
>> THE QUESTION:  Is there some way to ask Firefox for, say,
>> http://123.45.67.89:www.keithl.com/ , so that the browser goes
>> to the right IP address and Apache gets the right browser  
>> information,
>> as if DNS was actually pointing there?
>>
>> Yes, I can fake out the DNS on my own browser machine, but I would
>> like a technique that I can use on another machine that I do not
>> control, to make sure the new IP address is reachable before I change
>> the DNS server to point to it.
>
> On Thu, November 29, 2007 20:11, Tim Bruce said:
>>
>> Can't you just add the IP address in your local hosts file and  
>> assign it
>> to the DOMAIN NAME of your choice?
>>
>> Or am I missing something obvious or not understanding the problem?
>
> Read my last paragraph again.  Imagine I want to ask a dozen people to
> check the new server for accessability, address blockage, etc.  They
> are on Windoze, Macs, Solaris, etc.  They are running Explorer, Opera,
> Firefox, and Safari.  They don't have root access.  I would like to  
> give
> them some strange redirecting URL so they can see if they can connect
> to the new site, WITHOUT changing over the DNS or changing the Apache
> config AGAIN after the testing period is over.
>
>
> I suspect browsers don't have this kind of "testing" feature.

Some kind of do (But it's simply not for the lay user.)

> The
> HTTP protocols certainly permit it.

HTTP 1.1 and NamedVirtualHosts can make it a tad annoying, *but* you  
can make one change, in one config, and do much of this on the server  
side, and then give out the "magic URL", provided that the new site  
is at a new DocumentRoot on a new machine (or on the same machine  
with a new named virtual host entry, but that's a DNS change, too)....

Somebody hinted as using mod_proxy, which sounds like the perfect  
tool, in some ways....
-----
  ProxyRequests Off

<Proxy *>
Order deny,allow
Allow from all
</Proxy>

ProxyPass /sekrit http://123.45.67.89/

#Depending on how you want to mess with HTTP headers...
#ProxyPassReverse /sekrit http://www.keithl.com/
-----

http://www.keithl.com/sekrit now looks at a different server entirely  
for the content of that folder.

Unfortunately, this will *not* allow you to fully test SSL tunnels,  
or iptable based configs, because those are at the DNS->IP level.  
Without being able to control *other people's machines at the DNS  
level (got root?)*, the above is merely another way of simply asking  
them to check the site at:

http://123.45.67.89/

...with an intermediary server handling the request.

> But if browsers DO have this kind of feature, it would mean that there
> are at least some "computer scientists" who are actually  
> Scientists, who
> understand proper experimental methods, and design proper experimental
> tools.  If these rare ducks exist, and they have managed to get such a
> feature in some browsers, I would like to know how to access it.

https://addons.mozilla.org/en-US/firefox/addon/966
...Will allow you to change the HTTP 1.1 requested host name, while  
still talking to the same machine IP (again, if you don't control  
their DNS, you don't control what IP they request data from). It's  
not a tool for the lay user.

The reason *why* such tools are likely rare is that you're basically  
talking about adding in a shim layer, that mucks around with a  
machine's DNS results, and essentially *lies* to the browser about  
the right IP for a given DNS lookup. Such tools certainly *do* exist  
in the windows world..... mostly in the form of viruses and adware  
that hijack users from one requested IP to another. In general, it  
makes more sense for programmers to use an existing system API for  
DNS rather than create a DNS client (or an over-ride) inside of their  
browser code.

Putting my "evil" cap on, this question is not entirely different  
from asking "Without asking the users to change anything, and without  
making a special DNS test name in that (or any other) domain, how can  
I craft a URL to channel users from Paypal.com into my server, so  
they'll give me their login credentials?"

For many creative variations on that Paypal theme, I suggest viewing  
your local SPAM archives. ;)

-Bop
